# a
# map() function returns a map object(which is an iterator) of the results after
# applying the given function to each item of a given iterable (list, tuple etc.)
# syntax: map(fun, iter)
EXERCISE['Diet'] = list(map(lambda x: x.upper(), EXERCISE['Diet']))
EXERCISE

# b
EXERCISE.to_csv("Exercise.csv")

EXERCISE2 = pd.concat(chunk)
EXERCISE2

# cut - cut command creates equispaced bins but frequency of samples is unequal in each bin

EXERCISE['Pbin'] = pbin

09/02/2022, 22:42 - ğŸš©Abhishek Phulera: To the Vice Chancellor

Respected Sir

As you can see, there are some students from the union protesting for opening the colleges for offline classes, sir most of the protestors are the local students of Delhi some are not even students of the Delhi University , who are doing this just for the sake of politics.

We genuinely are the students of Delhi University who want the classes of this semester to be in online mode, even if you open the colleges it should be in the blended mode where both online and offline classes are given preference , as per the convenience of the students.

Moreover some students are from final year , who have just 2 more months left and therefore it would be difficult for them to arrange the accomodation. And it's in the best interest to continue the classes for the whole semester in the same manner they were started at the beginning. Half of the semester online and the other half offline is something that is just not favourable for the students residing outside Delhi.

09/02/2022, 22:47 - ğŸš©Abhishek Phulera: please copy paste the text and mail it to following email ID's:
 vc@du.ac.in
pvc@du.ac.in
dean_colleges@du.ac.in
registrar@du.ac.in
 dsw@du.ac.in
Greetings of the day,
Hope this mail finds you well. 
We are writing this mail on behalf of student body which is completely against college re-opening in mid-way. We do have justified reasons for demanding continuation on current mode of teaching for this semester. 

Our major reasons being:

1.	On online mode, it takes almost one and a half month for college to send readings to students in various states of country. We have just received our books, and itâ€™s difficult for an average student at this point to shift to another city and spend one month or so in the same, until we are just near the exams. 

2.	Students and their families are not mentally and economically prepared for physical shift to Delhi. If we consider two situations when, college goes offline after summer internship period so that we have enough time to choose PG and come to Delhi or if college reopens mid-way, itâ€™s having serious mental health impact on students and their capacity to focus on studies is highly reduced. Shifting will take time and lot of expenses with at this point of time in such short span our families are not ready for.

3.	Most of us engaged in others activities like coachings of competitive examinations because of online classes and now we cannot get our money back, which we have already invested. 

With utmost respect, we request the administration to understand our problem, and if reopening is considered, there should be continuation and option of online mode for students only for this semester, giving them time until next semester.

Thanking you in anticipation
Regards

16/02/2022, 14:19 - ğŸš©Abhishek Phulera: Legal Update:

The matter was heard today at Delhi High Court. Sr Advocate Sanjay Hegde sir represented the students. 

The Court was not inclined to entertain the petition but our issues were pressed by the Sr Adv Sanjay Hegde sir.

The Court was also disinclined to allow online exams.

The Counsel for DU raised objections on maintainability, locus, nature of Writ, PIL jurisdiction and others.

The Court noted that only around 20-24 working days are remaining in the semester, and asked the Counsel for DU if the classes can be conducted in Hybrid mode for the remainder of the semester.

The Counsel for DU has been given time to seek instructions (talk to DU) and file an affidavit.

The order of the notified offline exams scheduled has not been further assailed as the Court was not inclined to interfere with examination order.

The next hearing is scheduled on 22 Feb, 2022 (Tuesday) on the issues of classes.
